class=\"trb_embed_related_title\">Proposed border wall designs</span>      <div class=\"trb_embed_related_caption\"><p>Up to 400 companies are expected to submit proposals Tuesday to build President Donald Trump\u2019s proposed border wall.</p></div>      <div class=\"trb_embed_related_credit_and_caption\"><p>Up to 400 companies are expected to submit proposals Tuesday to build President Donald Trump\u2019s proposed border wall.</p></div></div>        </div></aside></div>\n          <div\n            ><div class=\"trb_ar_by\"\n      ><figure class=\"trb_ar_by_i_f\"><img src=\"http://www.trbimg.com/img-58000de8/turbine/sdut-phillip-molnar/70/70x70\" srcset=\"http://www.trbimg.com/img-58000de8/turbine/sdut-phillip-molnar/140/140x140 2x, http://www.trbimg.com/img-58000de8/turbine/sdut-phillip-molnar/210/210x210 3x\" alt=\"Phillip Molnar\" width=\"70\" height=\"70\" title=\"Phillip Molnar\" class=\"trb_ar_by_i\"></figure\n                  ><span class=\"trb_ar_by_nm_pm\"\n        ><span data-byline-withoutby class=\"trb_ar_by_nm_au\"><a itemprop=\"author\" href=\"/sdut-phillip-molnar-staff.html#nt=byline\" class=\"trb_ar_by_nm_au_a\">Phillip Molnar</a\n></span\n          ><span class=\"trb_ar_by_b\"></span\n      ><a class=\"trb_ar_by_cl\" href=\"mailto:phillip.molnar@sduniontribune.com?subject=Regarding: &quot;Trump&apos;s border wall just got real: The builders have submitted their plans&quot;\" data-role=\"sc_sEmail\">Contact Reporter</a\n    ></span\n    ></div\n  ><div class=\"trb_ar_dateline\"><time itemprop=\"datePublished\" class=\"trb_ar_dateline_time\" data-dt=\"April 4, 2017, 5:05 PM\" datetime=\"2017-04-04T17:05:00PDT\"></time>\n  </div>\n    </div>\n            <div itemprop=\"articleBody\">\n                    \n                        <div class=\"trb_ar_page\"  data-role=\"pagination_page\" data-content-page=\"1\">\n                          \n      <p>Imagine a border wall made of solar panels or a booby trap of nuclear waste where the United States meets Mexico.</p><p>Those were some of the proposals submitted by up to 450 companies that made the deadline Tuesday for bids to build the 2,000-mile wall along the Mexican border, a cornerstone of President Donald Trump\u2019s campaign.</p><div class=\"trb_gptAd trb_ar_main_ad\" data-role=\"adloader adloader_ad delayload delayload_done\" data-adloader-size=\"300x250\" data-state=\"adloader_unloaded\"  data-withinviewport-options=\"bottomOffset=100\"  data-adloader-position=\"articleCube\" data-adloader-adtype=\"articlebottomcube\" data-adloader-label ></div\n       >\n  <p>Roughly 20 companies will be chosen by the U.S. Department of Homeland Security and be invited to build prototype designs in San Diego County.</p><p>The wall has yet to be funded as Congress is expected to debate the upcoming budget for much of April. Trump had originally said he would get Mexico for the wall but has since pushed for federal spending to begin the process.</p><div class=\"trb_ar_cont\" data-ar-cont=\"Article continues below\"></div>\n            <aside class=\"trb_ar_sponsoredmod\" data-v-ymid=\"ym 1514378282637047879\" data-adloader-networktype=\"yieldmo\" data-role=\"delayload delayload_item\" data-screen-size='mobile' data-withinviewport-options=\"bottomOffset=100&topOffset=1000000\" data-load-method=\"trb.vendor.yieldmo.init\" data-load-type=\"method\" >\n            </aside><aside class=\"trb_ar_sponsoredmod trb_barker_mediaconductor\" data-adloader-networktype=\"mediaconductor\" data-role=\"delayload delayload_item\" data-screen-size='desktop' data-withinviewport-options=\"bottomOffset=100\" data-load-method=\"trb.vendor.mediaconductor.init\" data-load-type=\"method\"  data-vendor-mc></aside><p>U.S. Customs and Border Patrol said it will select bidders around June 1 and companies will build prototypes in San Diego County on federal land that month. The prototypes will be built within 120 feet of the border but the exact location has not been selected, according to <a href=\"http://hosted2.ap.org/APDEFAULT/386c25518f464186bf7a2ac026580ce7/Article_2017-04-04-US--Border%20Wall/id-25ca0f01a89246d5973174eafe91ba5d\" target=\"_blank\">The Associated Press</a>.</p><p><strong><a href=\"http://www.sandiegouniontribune.com/business/economy/sd-first-look-proposed-border-wall-designs-20170331-photogallery.html\" target=\"_blank\">RELATED: See the proposals for the Trump border wall</a></strong></p><p>The federal government has yet to confirm how many bidders submitted plans. More than 20 San Diego County companies had expressed interest in applying.</p><p>For James Carpenter, owner of Quantum Logistics in Mission, Texas, the Tuesday deadline was a welcome finish.</p><div class=\"trb_ar_cont\" data-ar-cont=\"Article continues below\"></div>\n  \t\t        \n                  <aside class=\"trb_ar_sponsoredmod\" data-adloader-networktype=\"yieldmo\" data-v-ymid=\"ym_1606468342064200017\" data-role=\"delayload delayload_item\"  data-withinviewport-options=\"bottomOffset=100\" data-load-method=\"trb.vendor.yieldmo.init\" data-load-type=\"method\" >\n                  </aside><p>\u201cI feel like I can get some sleep,\u201d he said Tuesday afternoon, on the phone from Kabul, Afghanistan, where his company is installing perimeter security for a Department of Defense site.</p><p>Carpenter, an Army veteran who served in Iraq and Afghanistan, said he started working on a wall<strong> </strong>design three months ago because he anticipated the federal government would be taking bids<strong>.</strong></p><p><strong><a href=\"http://www.sandiegouniontribune.com/news/border-baja-california/sd-me-barrier-walls-photogallery.html\" target=\"_blank\">SEE ALSO: 13 barrier walls and fences that came before Trump's</a></strong></p><p>He submitted designs for a concrete wall and a wall made of other materials, using strong materials to protect the barrier from a car bomb or suicide vest. His designs also use seismic sensors and drones to secure the wall.</p><p>\u201cEverybody else looks at this as a construction project,\u201d Carpenter said. \u201cI look at this from a security standpoint.\u201d</p><p>The Trump administration said winning bids must have a design that is 30 feet tall, can\u2019t be climbed and is constructed to prevent digging below the wall for at least 6 feet. The side facing the U.S. should be \u201caesthetically pleasing in color,\u201d the instructions said.</p><p>Many of the companies came up with unique solutions for the wall that went beyond what the federal government requested.</p><ul>\r\n\t<li>Manatts, a Johnston, Iowa-based contractor, proposed using the wall as an opportunity for engraving \u2014 from memorials to family trees \u2014 to pay for the wall. It said its research showed a high demand from Americans to engrave the wall and suggested a public-private partnership to get it done.</li>\r\n\t<li>National Consulting Service, of National City, proposed building a monorail on top of the wall that could help revitalize cities on both sides of the border.</li>\r\n\t<li>Gleason Partners, based in Las Vegas, designed a wall with massive solar panels to cut down on the cost to pay for the wall and infrastructure needs for the border patrol.</li>\r\n\t<li>Black Security Products, out of Austin, Texas, designed 4-inch spacing below the bottom of its system to allow animals to pass through, as well as a rip rap (loose stone system) so that water and some small species could traverse the wall.</li>\r\n</ul><p>Many of the larger companies bidding on the wall did not provide The San Diego Union-Tribune with copies of their designs because they are in competition with each other and do not want their efforts becoming public.</p><p>It is not clear if the government<strong> </strong>will release the designs to the public. Border Patrol spokesman Roger Maier said media and others interested should file a Freedom of Information Act request. (The Union-Tribune has filed a request for designs.)</p><p>Speaking to an unnamed U.S. official with knowledge of the plans, the AP said the government would spend $200,000 to $500,000 on each prototype and the Border Patrol (and local police) would establish a buffer zone at the San Diego County site where they are constructed.</p><p>Submitting a bid, let alone winning, can bring risks. Several Latino business owners have reported death threats since it became public they were bidding on the wall, said <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/wonk/wp/2017/03/29/these-hispanic-contractors-offered-to-build-trumps-border-wall-then-the-death-threats-began/?utm_term=.48a27388d1d6\" target=\"_blank\">The Washington Post</a>.</p><p>One local company, R.E. Staite Engineering of Barrio Logan, was the subject of a <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/events/212930012523688/\" target=\"_blank\">small protest</a> last week. One sign placed outside the business said, \u201cThis company is selling its soul.\u201d</p><p>Bidder Concrete Contractors Interstate, in San Diego County for more than 30 years, has 55 employees and many who are Latino. Owner Russ Baumgartner decided to ask his workers before putting in a bid.</p><p>\u201cThe overall response was, \u2018Our family comes first. If it keeps us busy, go for it\u2019,\u201d Baumgartner said.</p><p>Besides funding for the wall, other questions remain, such as how companies working on its construction will be protected and how small businesses will be included in its construction.</p><div class=\"trb_ar_cont\" data-ar-cont=\"Article continues below\"></div>\n  <aside class=\"trb_embed\"  data-content-size=\"large\" data-css-key=videoscroll>\n</script>\n</body>\n</html>", "title": "Trump's border wall just got real: The builders have submitted their plans", "url": "http://www.sandiegouniontribune.com/business/economy/sd-fi-border-wal-20170404-story.html", "date": "04-04-2017", "source": "latimes", "text": "Imagine a border wall made of solar panels or a booby trap of nuclear waste where the United States meets Mexico.\n\nThose were some of the proposals submitted by up to 450 companies that made the deadline Tuesday for bids to build the 2,000-mile wall along the Mexican border, a cornerstone of President Donald Trump\u2019s campaign.\n\nRoughly 20 companies will be chosen by the U.S. Department of Homeland Security and be invited to build prototype designs in San Diego County.\n\nThe wall has yet to be funded as Congress is expected to debate the upcoming budget for much of April. Trump had originally said he would get Mexico for the wall but has since pushed for federal spending to begin the process.\n\nU.S. Customs and Border Patrol said it will select bidders around June 1 and companies will build prototypes in San Diego County on federal land that month. The prototypes will be built within 120 feet of the border but the exact location has not been selected, according to The Associated Press.\n\nRELATED: See the proposals for the Trump border wall\n\nThe federal government has yet to confirm how many bidders submitted plans. More than 20 San Diego County companies had expressed interest in applying.\n\nFor James Carpenter, owner of Quantum Logistics in Mission, Texas, the Tuesday deadline was a welcome finish.\n\n\u201cI feel like I can get some sleep,\u201d he said Tuesday afternoon, on the phone from Kabul, Afghanistan, where his company is installing perimeter security for a Department of Defense site.\n\nCarpenter, an Army veteran who served in Iraq and Afghanistan, said he started working on a wall design three months ago because he anticipated the federal government would be taking bids.\n\nSEE ALSO: 13 barrier walls and fences that came before Trump's\n\nHe submitted designs for a concrete wall and a wall made of other materials, using strong materials to protect the barrier from a car bomb or suicide vest. His designs also use seismic sensors and drones to secure the wall.\n\n\u201cEverybody else looks at this as a construction project,\u201d Carpenter said. \u201cI look at this from a security standpoint.\u201d\n\nThe Trump administration said winning bids must have a design that is 30 feet tall, can\u2019t be climbed and is constructed to prevent digging below the wall for at least 6 feet. The side facing the U.S. should be \u201caesthetically pleasing in color,\u201d the instructions said.\n\nMany of the companies came up with unique solutions for the wall that went beyond what the federal government requested.\n\nManatts, a Johnston, Iowa-based contractor, proposed using the wall as an opportunity for engraving \u2014 from memorials to family trees \u2014 to pay for the wall. It said its research showed a high demand from Americans to engrave the wall and suggested a public-private partnership to get it done.\n\nNational Consulting Service, of National City, proposed building a monorail on top of the wall that could help revitalize cities on both sides of the border.\n\nGleason Partners, based in Las Vegas, designed a wall with massive solar panels to cut down on the cost to pay for the wall and infrastructure needs for the border patrol.\n\nBlack Security Products, out of Austin, Texas, designed 4-inch spacing below the bottom of its system to allow animals to pass through, as well as a rip rap (loose stone system) so that water and some small species could traverse the wall.\n\nMany of the larger companies bidding on the wall did not provide The San Diego Union-Tribune with copies of their designs because they are in competition with each other and do not want their efforts becoming public.\n\nIt is not clear if the government will release the designs to the public. Border Patrol spokesman Roger Maier said media and others interested should file a Freedom of Information Act request. (The Union-Tribune has filed a request for designs.)\n\nSpeaking to an unnamed U.S. official with knowledge of the plans, the AP said the government would spend $200,000 to $500,000 on each prototype and the Border Patrol (and local police) would establish a buffer zone at the San Diego County site where they are constructed.\n\nSubmitting a bid, let alone winning, can bring risks. Several Latino business owners have reported death threats since it became public they were bidding on the wall, said The Washington Post.\n\nOne local company, R.E. Staite Engineering of Barrio Logan, was the subject of a small protest last week. One sign placed outside the business said, \u201cThis company is selling its soul.\u201d\n\nBidder Concrete Contractors Interstate, in San Diego County for more than 30 years, has 55 employees and many who are Latino. Owner Russ Baumgartner decided to ask his workers before putting in a bid.\n\n\u201cThe overall response was, \u2018Our family comes first. If it keeps us busy, go for it\u2019,\u201d Baumgartner said.\n\nBesides funding for the wall, other questions remain, such as how companies working on its construction will be protected and how small businesses will be included in its construction.\n\nCaption EpiPen recall expands The products can be replaced for free by contacting: (877) 650-3494 or customer.service@mylan.com.
